# Excalidraw Data
## Text Elements
Part 1. Snell's Law ^Ul3MKcuL

1. We set up the prism perpendicular to the incident bean 
2. We increased theta to 10 degrees and measured theta for the outgoing beam.The angle of the outgoing beam was 25 degrees.
3. The work for using Snell's Law to calculate the theoretical outgoing theta is shown below: ^Cv9MjExg

In essence, any incoming light at an angle of 10 degrees to its normal will be turned an extra beta prime degrees. So, if the incoming light is re-framed to be zero degrees, the reading will be 45 degrees ^qX2zL5G7

Part Two: Total Internal Reflection ^3EcFZNbH

1. We set the beam angle to zero and observed that the prism undergoes total internal reflection with no escaped light.
2. We increased the beam angle until we observed the limit at which light escaped. This critical angle was 6 degrees.
3. The calculation of the theoretical critical angle is shown below: ^H1ms4b4Q

Our measurement had a 1.18 percent error. ^KvOFf0Fo

Our error is 8.9 percent.
 ^ipuZfA5u

Part Three: Fresnel Equations and Brewster Angle ^X6aqEN9y

For simplicity's sake, we will first calculate Brewster's Angle.
 ^CM1xJVbB

TM: ^gJkaIKNa

TE: ^prBNRUfX

:Reflectance Plot: ^norUoNqK

We have approximately a 7 percent error assuming that we average the angle at the minimum intensity value to be 60 degrees. ^lZwDumnD
